## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, a core problem in solid mechanics and materials science. Temperature typically softens materials (reducing modulus and yield strength), while the stress-strain relationship can be linear, power-law hardening, or exhibit more complex nonlinear behavior.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law with T-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic deformation)
- Ramberg-Osgood (inverted form): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * epsilon)**c3 (nonlinear stress-strain with hardening transition)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T)**c3 (flow stress with strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Thermally-activated flow: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (exponential thermal softening combined with power-law hardening)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturation hardening with temperature-dependent saturation stress)
- Neo-Hookean rubber elasticity: sigma = c0 * T * (epsilon - c1 * epsilon**c2) (entropic elasticity where modulus is proportional to T)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic expansion)
- Linear thermal softening with hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (power-law hardening with linearly T-dependent prefactor)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart type creep model inverted)
- Swift hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (1 + c3 * T) (Swift law with thermal correction)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (linear plus power-law hardening)
- Entropic elasticity: sigma = c0 * T * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**2) (rubber-like with temperature-proportional modulus)
- Thermal activation model: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 + T)**c3 (power-law dependence on both strain and temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening → Stress prefactor decreasing with T: multiplicative factor (1 - c*T), (T_ref/T)**c, or exp(-c*T)
- Entropic elasticity (rubber-like) → Modulus proportional to absolute temperature: sigma ~ c*T*f(epsilon)
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type exponential approach: (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicating dislocation saturation
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**n with 0 < n < 1 (Hollomon/Ludwik behavior in metals)
- Yield offset / initial strain → (epsilon + epsilon_0)**n form (Swift hardening, accounting for prior plastic strain)
- Separable temperature-strain dependence → sigma = g(T) * f(epsilon), where thermal and mechanical effects factorize
- Polynomial nonlinearity in strain → odd powers (epsilon, epsilon**3) for symmetric tension-compression behavior
- Hyperbolic sine stress dependence → sinh(c*sigma) appears in creep/viscoplastic flow, may invert to arcsinh form

If c4=0, exp(T·c4)=1, giving c0·ε + c1·ε^c2 + c3·ε. No T dependence. Can't match.

Candidate 105 verdict: [NO MATCH] (confirmed)

Hmm, I realize the fundamental issue: GT is quadratic in T, meaning it has T² terms. Almost all candidates are either linear in T, have exp(T), or have T² only in rational form with (c1+ε) denominator.

Let me re-examine the rational T² candidates more carefully. The key question is whether ε·T² + ε·T + ε² + ε can be expressed as combinations of ε²/(c1+ε)·T² + ε/(c1+ε)·T² + ... etc.

For the rational candidates with T², the general form after setting c1=0 gives polynomial terms. But the issue is that the T² coefficient is always ε (from ε²/ε) or constant (from ε/ε), and we need the T coefficient to be proportional to ε as well.

Let me re-examine **Candidate 8** more carefully:

T²·c0·ε²/(c1+ε) + T²·c2·ε/(c1+ε) + T·c3·ε/(c1+ε) + T·c4·ε²/(c1+ε) + c5·ε/(c1+ε) + c6·ε²/(c1+ε)

Factor out 1/(c1+ε):
= [T²·(c0·ε² + c2·ε) + T·(c3·ε + c4·ε²) + c5·ε + c6·ε²] / (c1+ε)

GT = A·ε·T² + B·ε·T + C·ε² + D·ε = ε·(A·T² + B·T + D) + C·ε²

For the rational expression to equal this polynomial, we need (c1+ε) to divide the numerator, or c1=0.

With c1=0:
= T²·(c0·ε + c2) + T·(c3 + c4·ε) + c5 + c6·ε

GT = A·ε·T² + B·ε·T + C·ε² + D·ε

Matching T² coefficient: c0·ε + c2 = A·ε → c0 = A, c2 = 0
Matching T coefficient: c3 + c4·ε = B·ε → c3 = 0, c4 = B
Matching T⁰: c5 + c6·ε = C·ε² + D·ε → c6 = D, c5 = 0, but we need C·ε² and there's no ε² term!

So Candidate 8 can give: A·ε·T² + B·ε·T + D·ε but NOT C·ε². Missing ε².

Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH] (confirmed)

**Candidate 98 re-examination:**
T²·c0·ε²/(c1+ε) + T²·c2·ε/(c1+ε) + T·c3·ε/(c1+ε) + c4·ε/(c1+ε) + c5·ε²/(c1+ε) + c6·ε³/(c1+ε)

With c1=0:
T²·c0·ε + T²·c2 + T·c3 + c4 + c5·ε + c6·ε²

Need: A·ε·T² + B·ε·T + C·ε² + D·ε

T² coeff: c0·ε + c2 = A·ε → c0=A, c2=0
T coeff: c3 = B·ε → impossible since c3 is constant!

So can't match. Confirmed [NO MATCH].

**Candidate 99 re-examination:**
With c1=0: T²·c0·ε + T²·c2 + T·c3·ε + c4 + c5·ε²

T² coeff: c0·ε + c2 = A·ε → c0=A, c2=0
T coeff: c3·ε = B·ε → c3=B ✓
T⁰: c4 + c5·ε² = C·ε² + D·ε → c5=C, c4=0, but missing D·ε!

So Candidate 99 gives: A·ε·T² + B·ε·T + C·ε² but NOT D·ε. Missing the ε term.

D = 6.266345·342.1714² ≈ 733,686 which is very large and non-zero.

Candidate 99 verdict: [NO MATCH] (confirmed)

Hmm, what about keeping c1 ≠ 0? Let me think about this differently.

For any rational candidate with denominator (c1+ε), the expression is a rational function of ε (for fixed T). But GT is a polynomial in ε (for fixed T). A rational function equals a polynomial only if the denominator divides the numerator. This means either c1=0 (trivial case) or the numerator has (c1+ε) as a factor.

Let me try Candidate 99 with c1 ≠ 0:
[T²·c0·ε² + T²·c2·ε + T·c3·ε² + c4·ε + c5·ε³] / (c1+ε)

For this to be a polynomial, (c1+ε) must divide the numerator. Setting ε = -c1:
T²·c0·c1² - T²·c2·c1 + T·c3·c1² - c4·c1 - c5·c1³ = 0 for all T.

This gives:
- T² coefficient: c0·c1² - c2·c1 = 0 → c2 = c0·c1
- T coefficient: c3·c1² = 0 → c3 = 0 or c1 = 0
- constant: -c4·c1 - c5·c1³ = 0 → c4 = -c5·c1²

If c1 ≠ 0, then c3 = 0. So the T coefficient in the result would be 0. But GT has non-zero B·ε·T. So this doesn't work either.

Wait, let me redo the polynomial division. If (c1+ε) divides the numerator, then:
Numerator = (c1+ε)·Q(ε,T) where Q is a polynomial.

Numerator = T²·c0·ε² + T²·c2·ε + T·c3·ε² + c4·ε + c5·ε³

With c2 = c0·c1, c3 = 0, c4 = -c5·c1²:
= T²·c0·ε² + T²·c0·c1·ε + c5·ε³ - c5·c1²·ε
= T²·c0·ε·(ε + c1) + c5·ε·(ε² - c1²)
= T²·c0·ε·(ε + c1) + c5·ε·(ε + c1)·(ε - c1)
= (ε + c1)·[T²·c0·ε + c5·ε·(ε - c1)]
= (ε + c1)·ε·[T²·c0 + c5·(ε - c1)]

So the result = ε·[c0·T² + c5·ε - c5·c1] = c0·ε·T² + c5·ε² - c5·c1·ε

This gives: A·ε·T² + C·ε² + D·ε with A=c0, C=c5, D=-c5·c1.

But GT also needs B·ε·T term. Since c3=0 was forced, there's no ε·T term. So still can't match.

Candidate 99 verdict: [NO MATCH] (triple confirmed)

Let me try **Candidate 100** with c1 ≠ 0:
[T²·c0·ε² + T²·c2·ε + T·c3·ε² + c4·ε] / (c1+ε)

Setting ε = -c1:
T²·c0·c1² - T²·c2·c1 + T·c3·c1² - c4·c1 = 0 for all T.

T²: c0·c1² - c2·c1 = 0 → c2 = c0·c1
T: c3·c1² = 0 → c3 = 0 (if c1≠0)
const: -c4·c1 = 0 → c4 = 0

Result = ε·[c0·T²] = c0·ε·T². Only one term. Can't match.

**Candidate 97** with c1 ≠ 0:

**Candidate 8** with c1 ≠ 0:

Numerator = T²·c0·ε·(ε+c1) + ε·[c5·ε + c6·ε² + (c5·c1-c6·c1²)]

I'm now going to look at this problem differently. The GT has the structure:
f(ε,T) = c0·ε² + c2·ε·(T-c3)²

Actually, I realize I should look at candidates where T appears in a squared form like (T-c)².

Candidate 59 verdict: [NO MATCH] (confirmed)

At this point, I've exhausted all candidates with T² dependence. None can produce the required B·ε·T term alongside the T² term.

GT = 2.354·ε² + 6.266·ε·(T - 342.17)²

Could any candidate with exp, cos, sin, or log somehow match this exactly? No - these are transcendental functions and can't equal a polynomial for all values.

Could any candidate with only T (linear) match? No - GT is quadratic in T.

Wait, I should double-check candidates with T^c0 more carefully.

I've confirmed c1=0 gives: T²·c0·ε + T·c4·ε + c6·ε (missing ε²)

Now what about **Candidate 98** which has additional ε²/(c1+ε) and ε³/(c1+ε) terms?

With c1=0: T²·c0·ε + T²·c2 + T·c3 + c4 + c5·ε + c6·ε² (has unwanted T², T, constant terms)

With c1=0 and c2=0, c3=0, c4=0: c0·ε·T² + c5·ε + c6·ε² (missing ε·T)

So Candidate 98 can produce 3 of 4 terms but always misses one.

Hmm, what about combining both approaches? With c1≠0, I showed the T-linear term vanishes. With c1=0, the T-linear term is a constant (not ε·T). Neither works.

Let me now look at the remaining candidates I haven't checked:

**Candidate 42:** T·c0·cos(c1·ε) + T·c2·ε²/(c3+ε) + c4·ε³ + c5·exp(T·c6) + c7·ε³/(c3+ε)

Has exp(T·c6). If c6=0, exp=1. Then: T·[c0·cos(c1·ε) + c2·ε²/(c3+ε)] + c4·ε³ + c5 + c7·ε³/(c3+ε). Linear in T. Can't match T².

Candidate 42 verdict: [NO MATCH] (confirmed)

**Candidate 43:** Very complex. Linear in T.

Candidate 43 verdict: [NO MATCH] (confirmed)

I believe I've now checked all 110 candidates. None of them can produce the GT expression which requires four independent basis functions: ε·T², ε·T, ε², and ε.

The fundamental issue is:
- Candidates with T² terms (8, 9, 22, 58-64, 88-89, 97-100) all have rational structure that prevents simultaneously having both ε·T² and ε·T terms.
- Candidates linear in T can't produce T².
- Candidates with exp(T·c) can't match polynomial T² dependence.
- Candidates with T^c0 (like 59, 79) have T^c0 in all or some terms, but can't independently produce both T² and T terms.

Actually wait - I need to re-examine **Candidate 59** more carefully:

T^c0·c1·ε²/(c2+ε) + T^c0·c3·ε/(c2+ε) + c4·ε/(c2+ε)

What if c0 is NOT an integer? Well, GT needs T² and T terms. T^c0 gives only one power of T. Can't produce two different powers.

What about candidates where T appears in fundamentally different ways?

**Candidate 8** has T² and T. Let me reconsider whether there's a way to get ε² from it.

Candidate 8: [T²·(c0·ε² + c2·ε) + T·(c3·ε + c4·ε²) + c5·ε + c6·ε²] / (c1+ε)

What if I don't require this to be a polynomial? The GT IS a polynomial. So the candidate must equal a polynomial. For a rational function to equal a polynomial everywhere, the denominator must divide the numerator (or c1=0).

I've shown both cases fail to produce all 4 terms simultaneously.

Let me try one more thing with Candidate 8. What if I allow c1 to be complex? No, constants must be real.

OK, I'm now confident that none of the 110 candidates match the GT.

Actually, wait. Let me reconsider some candidates more carefully. Let me look at candidates that might produce (T-c)² through squaring.

**Candidate 16:** T·c0·(c1+ε)² + c2·exp(c3·ε) + c4·(c5+ε)³ + c6·(c1+ε)²

= (c0·T + c6)·(c1+ε)² + c2·exp(c3·ε) + c4·(c5+ε)³

This is linear in T. The (c1+ε)² is a function of ε, not T.

**Candidate 18:** (c0·T + c5)·(c1+ε)^c2 + c3·ε/(c4+ε)

Linear in T.

None of these have (T-c)² structure.

Hmm, what about **Candidate 62**?
T²·c0·ε²/(c1+ε) + T²·c2·ε/(c1+ε) + c3·ε/(c1+ε) + c4·(c5+ε)^c6/(c1+ε)

With c1=0: T²·c0·ε + T²·c2 + c3 + c4·(c5+ε)^c6/ε

The last term has 1/ε which is problematic. Set c4=0: T²·c0·ε + T²·c2 + c3. Set c2=0, c3=0: c0·ε·T². Missing everything.

With c5=0, c6=2: c4·ε²/ε = c4·ε. Then with c2=0, c3=0: c0·ε·T² + c4·ε. Still missing ε·T and ε².

With c5=0, c6=3: c4·ε³/ε = c4·ε². Then: c0·ε·T² + c4·ε². Missing ε·T and ε.

Can't get all 4 terms.

Candidate 62 verdict: [NO MATCH] (confirmed)

I'm now truly confident. Let me verify my conclusion by checking if any candidate has the right "degrees of freedom" to match.

GT has 4 independent basis functions in (ε,T): {ε·T², ε·T, ε², ε}

For a candidate to match, it needs at least 4 free parameters AND the right functional form to span these 4 basis functions.

None of the 110 candidates can simultaneously produce ε·T² and ε·T as independent terms while also having ε² and ε.
